# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
Not x --> 0 ^m1Ge9bjc

Examples of Removable Discontinuities:
Holes ^xouO6jw2

Examples of Non-Removable Discontinuities:
- Asymptotes
- Jumps ^WmpeVgOf

Some removable values are ^tQFNLnFG

x = 4 is not removable because it is a jump ^KRxIej8O

to make the function continuous, f(3) has to be = 3 and not = 2 ^oWLZmtwL

f has a limit as x approaches -1 because the right hand and left-hand limit are equal
f has a limit as x approaches 0 because the right hand and left-hand limit are equal
f does not have a limit as x approaches 1 because the right hand and left-hand limit are unequal ^6dZ6s1y1

f is continuous at x = -1 because the left hand and right hand limits are equal, and f(-1) is equal to the limit
f is not continuous at x = 0 because f(0) is not equal to the limit
f is not continuous at x = 1 because the right-hand limit is not equal to the left-hand limit ^PuWtAG8S

Slope of normal line is Negative reciprocal of slope of tangent line ^VTTiZn1z

when k(x) is horizontal the tangent slope is = 0 ^hZoiXWo2

as x approaches -1, y has no bounds
 ^AErU96mw
